Postponing Review for the Second Batch of Personnel

The Shanghai Municipal Committee for Reviewing the Qualifications of Party Ideology Teachers previously submitted questions about the review regulations to the Municipal Party Committee, which forwarded them to the Central Training Department for clarification. (2) Amend the "Organizational Regulations of the Shanghai Municipal Committee for Reviewing the Qualifications of Party Ideology Teachers." (3) Amend the committee's rules of procedure and meeting rules. (4) Abolish the "Measures for Reviewing the Qualifications of Party Ideology Teachers in Shanghai." (5) Revise the detailed standards for determining qualifications. The above five proposals will be combined and submitted to the Municipal Executive Committee for filing. (6) The application for reviewing substitute Party Ideology Teachers was rejected. (7) The request to reconsider the qualifications of the first batch of qualified personnel was rejected. (8) Based on the Central Training Department's interpretation, the second batch of qualified personnel will be re-examined. The resolution is that two people temporarily retained by the Central Training Department should be eliminated, and five others should be eliminated. (9) Committee member Wang proposed supplementing the passing of the second batch of reviewed personnel, which was passed separately. (10) As the review period is approaching, and applications are increasing, it was resolved to extend the deadline for twenty days until September 30th. It is reported that after the new regulations and rules are approved, the review of the first batch of personnel will begin actively. The first batch of qualified personnel are currently filling out qualification certificates and will be announced soon.

Free Talk

Today's Words

Sixty 98

— Shou Juan

People who live to sixty years old can certainly be considered old. In the eyes of modern young people, they deserve to be scolded as "old but not dead" and be subject to slogans of overthrow. However, I think otherwise. I want to stand up for the elderly and defend them. Let's compare young people and old people. Which one has richer experience? Which one has more sufficient reason? Which one has a clearer understanding of the ways of the world? Young people will definitely disagree and retort, "Even if old people have richer experience, sufficient reason, and a relatively clear understanding of the ways of the world, their energy declines. What can they do?" I say, "That's not true either. Throughout ancient and modern Chinese and foreign history, there have been many who achieved great things in their old age. For example, the famous generals in the modern European war, such as Foch and Joffre of France, Haig of England, and Hindenburg of Germany, worked hard on the battlefield and served the country, all of whom were over sixty years old. And the great American inventor Edison, even in his old age, was still diligently inventing new things. They are not only "old but not dead," but also "old but strong."

Life at sixty has completed one cycle of the zodiac. From the age of sixty-one, it is like returning to youth and becoming a newborn baby. All kinds of heavy responsibilities await him to shoulder, and all kinds of great undertakings await him to establish. His bright future is truly immeasurable. Today is the first day of this newspaper's 60th anniversary, and it is also like returning to youth and becoming a newborn baby. On the one hand, it does not slack off because of its age. It relies on its boldness and determination to continue its struggle to overcome obstacles. I would like to use the words "old but not dead" and "old but strong" to wish it a long life.

A Record of Japanese Prime Minister Hamaguchi 99

— Wang Yanjin

The former Japanese Prime Minister Hamaguchi Yuko was also the president of the Minseitō. He was a reformer in politics and his ideas were novel, so he was admired by the people of his country. However, due to the global trend, the state of Japan's economic downturn did not decrease, and the number of unemployed people increased day by day. All of those folks blamed Mr. Hamaguchi. Thus, he was assassinated at Tokyo Station. Although he did not die on the spot, how could a sixty-year-old man endure such a great injury? He passed away on August 26. Fellow student Matsuda Yujiro is the beloved nephew of Mr. Hamaguchi's wife, Natsuko. He learned of Mr. Hamaguchi's situation in great detail. He occasionally talked about it after class. This is a record of the true story.

Childhood Mr. Hamaguchi's father, Yoshidate, was a pioneer of the Japanese Restoration. He treated his children very strictly. However, Mr. Hamaguchi had a playful nature and was lazy in his studies. Although he was repeatedly scolded, it was difficult to achieve results. Yoshidate was worried about this. It happened that his hometown of Koishikawa Kuseyama had a poor harvest for many years. The nearby residents all entered Mr. Hamaguchi's household as retainers and depended on him for a living. A certain farmer had a son who was young and eager to learn. Yoshidate valued him and adopted him as his son. He clothed him in fine clothes and fed him delicious food. Mr. Hamaguchi, on the other hand, wore his worn-out clothes and ate his leftover grain. He looked emaciated and was very unhappy. He cried to his mother and said, "Why does Father favor him and abandon me?" His mother said, "It is better to have no son than to have a son like you." Mr. Hamaguchi turned over a new leaf from then on and concentrated on his studies, progressing step by step, and eventually achieved success. It cannot be said that this was not due to his family's teaching.

Student days Mr. Hamaguchi studied in the Department of Politics at the Imperial University. He had never touched books on political science on weekdays. However, those who buried themselves in the library all day were pondering Chinese history and Western history. When classmates asked him, he did not hide anything and answered eloquently, "History is politics, and it is also the politics of the past. We scholars of politics should first understand the politics of the past and then attach it to the politics of the present. Only then can we produce the politics of the future." His insights were so remarkable.

Reign In response to the needs of the times, the Minseitō was organized. Mr. Hamaguchi spared no effort in recruiting party members. Within a few years, its influence spread throughout the three islands. Last year, in the aftermath of Tanaka Giichi's tyrannical government, Mr. Hamaguchi was elected Prime Minister after winning the election. He became even more energetic and planned to implement the salary reduction and the three major reorganization plans. He pondered deeply and thoroughly. Whenever he became mentally exhausted, he frequently struck his head. His family advised him not to suffer so much. Mr. Hamaguchi often chuckled and did not stop. It is said that he only ate two meals a day and slept only five hours.

Li the Cobbler 100

— Yan Qian

There was a cobbler named Li in Shaoxing, about thirty years old. He claimed to be from Wu County, but he did not speak entirely in the Wu dialect. His accent was a mix of various sounds, indicating that he had traveled extensively. Li set up a stall at the entrance of the house, and in addition to mending shoes for people, he also made rough shoes for sale. Every day at dusk, he would be seen holding a book, his eyes fixed on it. He was very diligent. When he was in the mood to talk, he would talk to people about the past and present, up and down, in great detail and with great interest. He always made the listeners reluctant to leave. One day, a certain Jia, dressed like a student, came to buy shoes. Seeing a book titled "Essentials of Sociology" placed on the shoe rack, he rashly said, "Do you also know how to read?" Li humbly replied, "It's just a casual pastime. I have read this book once before. There are some places that I have not fully understood, so I am studying it again." As he spoke, he vividly described the meaning of the book, unable to stop himself. Jia stared straight at him with wide eyes, hesitated, and then retreated. It is said that he did not buy the shoes either.

Xu and Wang Collaborate on Refugee Paintings 101

— Sun Choucheng

Xu Shiying and Wang Yiting, permanent members of the Shanghai Fundraising Committee for Emergency Relief of Flood Disasters in Various Provinces, because of the flood this year, besides the government's allocation of funds for relief, relied entirely on the enthusiastic donations of people from all walks of life. They specially collaborated on paintings of refugees, depicting the disaster situation on white paper, with accompanying poems and lyrics, in order to print and distribute them to all walks of life, to make people feel horrified and encourage donations. The following excerpts are from their meanings, for the enjoyment of readers and to promote publicity.

Screen painting The painting depicts a vast expanse of water. The drowned people either only have their heads exposed and are still crying for help, or have already died and are floating on the surface of the water. On a high place, a person stands upright, looking down at the tragic scene in the water. His eyebrows are tightly locked, and he is helpless. There is a poem of seven quatrains, saying, "A painting of refugees by Zheng Xia. Wherever Geng Gui arrives, he calls for the people. Try to observe the continuous state of hardship. Drowning and starving are also due to fate." There is also a note of four large characters: "Save lives, save lives." Attached to the postscript is: "The flood disaster in various provinces this year is extremely severe. The number of displaced people is unknown. I implore those who have the power to donate and plant blessings widely." Written by Bailongshan on August 20th.

Vertical axis About four feet long. The painting depicts dozens of people drowned in the water country, all of whom have died. In the distance, the top of a large tree is exposed in the water, with seven or eight people perched on it. They all have emaciated faces and are holding children, who are crying. There are two poems of seven quatrains, saying, "Rain and wind suddenly came. In an instant, the water rose and submerged the building. No clothes, no food, and no shelter. Selling daughters and sons, crying sadly. The mainland is sinking, and the lives of the people are hanging in the balance. Who has the power to turn the tide? Now it is easy to plant blessings and reap the harvest. Try to buy a thousand gold to continue the life field." Underneath is written "Xinwei New Autumn. Flood disasters in various provinces. For the writing of refugee paintings, several numbers of the Bailongshan people."

Folding fan There is also a folding fan, prepared to be sent to Mr. Zhu Qichen, who is going to Hankou for disaster relief. On one side is recorded a poem of seven quatrains on the flood, written by Xu Shiying: "Fish under the bed, frogs on the curtain. Boat in front of the steps, car in the room. It is even more pitiful that the thatched hut is completely submerged. Only the displaced are seen, not the homes." On the other side is painted a boat, with two people inside, rescuing the disaster victims in the water. It is titled: "Traveling the road is more difficult than the road to Shu. Floating and sinking in the city, this turbulent wave. Manjushri's great vow is like a boat. May all sentient beings be safe in the high places." There is also a postscript saying: "Xinwei New Autumn. Flood disasters in various provinces. Hankou is especially severe. Mr. Qichen made a great vow to help the living. The Relief Society is raising funds. Mr. Qichen went to save them, sparing no effort. It is admirable. I made this to give as a gift. Wang Zhen."

Reading the "Shen Bao" Anniversary Issue, the Maiden 102

—

Records of What I Saw and Heard in the Old Capital 103

— Zhu An

My friend Zhu, his pen has a flying charm, and every time he depicts scenery, it makes people feel as if they are there, enjoying the scenery and taking care of each other, fearing that the end of the chapter will come. His writing takes shape with the object, and when he encounters a garden, he becomes a jade, like the clouds in the sky, rising and stopping unintentionally, and naturally becoming interesting. It is thought that he writes directly with his pen, without any intention. Only when the heart is free and the hands are idle can it be like this. Those who read his writing always become one with him. Du Lao's poem says, "Satisfaction is related to flying movement, and the end of the chapter is connected to the vastness." This cannot be said by those who are not good at writing, nor can it be said by those who are not good at reading. Mr. Zhu's writing is quite worthy of this. His writing includes poetry, novels, and travel notes. In ancient times, there was Li Daoyuan, in recent times, Liu Zihou, and again, the Tang Dynasty novels. One day, he mentioned the beauty of the customs and objects of the old capital and persuaded me to visit. Therefore, I wanted to imitate Lu Shilong's theory and Zhong, Bao Mingyuan's record of Lei An, to quickly express the meaning of Tu Da and chew. I held the pen for several nights and completed dozens of chapters, but I still could not stop myself. I accepted and read it, and praised it greatly, saying that there has never been such a refined and beautiful work of guidance. The above few words are written to invite others to share the same appreciation. Recorded by Chunhen on a summer day in the year 20.

燕姬 104

The Miscellaneous Records of Yanjing says: (Women in the capital do not know how to weave. They spend their days applying cosmetics and binding their feet, buying meat, noodles, fruits, and other things, eating greedily as they please. Their families are impoverished. But when they go out, they are adorned with pearls and jewels, wearing fashionable clothes that fit them perfectly, appearing to be of great status). The Remnants of the Old Capital says: (Inside, there is no store of grain, but outside, there are silk and satin garments). This is because officials, gentry, clerks, and soldiers from the Ming and Qing dynasties lived here, cultivating a frivolous and decadent atmosphere. The Manchu women of the late Qing dynasty were especially criticized. Once the country was lost and their homes were destroyed, they had neither the skills to make a living nor the training to work hard. Therefore, the older ones were reduced to being servants, and the young ones were reduced to selling their smiles. Their situation was extremely pitiful. The reason for this was not something that happened overnight. Manchu women paid no attention to women's work, as mentioned above. Even in terms of adornment, they were inferior to Han women. In the past, they all combed their hair into high buns, several inches wide, made with false hair, completely losing their natural beauty, and added thick layers of makeup, creating a vulgar and gaudy appearance. Since the relocation of the palace in the thirteenth year of the Republic, this decoration has no longer been seen. Instead, they imitate Han makeup, earning them the ridicule of "imitating Handan." The ancients said that Yan and Zhao had many beautiful women, but this saying is no longer applicable today. However, Manchu women have one thing that Han women cannot match. Those from noble families are accustomed to etiquette. Their responses, advances, and retreats, their movements, and their demeanor are all within the bounds of propriety, dignified and poised. This is almost impossible to learn through mere study. Europeans value social women, and consider shyness and awkwardness shameful. This style is seen in Manchu women. They inherently possess this beautiful quality. If their pride and laziness are removed, and modern cosmetic techniques are added, they are certainly sufficient to be model women. The most beautiful of the Manchu women are often seen. It is only that they are slightly clumsy in applying makeup. Their attire is also superior to that of Han women. Therefore, the qipao has not been abandoned to this day and is instead considered convenient.

城圯誌異 105

— By Shi Yan

During the continuous heavy rain a few days ago, many sections of our city walls collapsed. There are two particularly strange events in this, which I record to tell the readers.

When the city tower at the Great North Gate collapsed, it was about eleven in the morning. There was a continuous stream of people passing under the city wall. The collapse was so extensive that it took two days to remove all the bricks and stones. Yet, no one was injured. This is most strange. When the city tower fell, a huge brick first fell to the ground. Those who saw it told each other in alarm, "The city wall is about to collapse! Avoid it and don't walk there!" Therefore, those who were entering and exiting all ran away and stood at a distance to watch what would happen. As expected, in less than five minutes, there was a loud crash, and the entire structure collapsed. If there had not been a brick falling first, the pedestrians would never have expected the city wall to collapse and would have continued to enter and exit as usual. A tragic scene would have been unimaginable. Therefore, the falling of this brick was like the alarm bell of a fire truck, causing people to flee and avoid danger.

Another family lived close to the city wall. They were villagers who had come to the city to pay taxes and live there out of fear of bandits. During the continuous rain, a crack of about a foot had appeared in the city wall behind their house during the day, indicating that it was about to collapse. People advised them to move quickly. However, the villagers remained calm and went to bed that night. Unexpectedly, disaster struck at midnight. The city wall collapsed from above, completely covering their house. Under a toppled nest, how can there be unbroken eggs? Four out of the five family members died. Fortunately, the survivor was a child of only three or four years old. The villagers had come to the city out of fear of bandits, but now they lost their lives trying to escape them. How lamentable! What is strange is this surviving child. In the village, the child had been kidnapped by bandits. The bandits threatened to kill the child when their demands were not met. However, when they fired a gun, the bullet missed the child and killed one of the bandits. They shot again, but still missed. The bandits found this strange and spared the child's life. Later, the child was finally redeemed with gold. When the family returned home, they all came to the city to seek refuge, entering a haven. When the city wall collapsed this time, the child was lying in his mother's arms. The mother fell from the bed to the ground. The child followed down, but the child had been under the mother's arm. Thus, they happened to be protected by the mother's arm. The mother was instantly killed by the pressure of the wood and stones. The child was unharmed thanks to the arch formed by the mother's arm, which prevented the child from being crushed. Therefore, when they were excavated the next morning, the child was still safe and sound. Everyone said that this child did not die at the hands of bandits and did not die under the collapsed city wall. As the saying goes, "He who survives a great disaster is sure to have good fortune in the future." This child will surely have a great future. It is truly a miracle.

Narratives and Discussion Society

The Husband's Wife (1) 106

— By Jiang Hongjiao

"You fool! Why do you care about other people's business so much? Why do you have to be so earnest?" Mrs. Chen felt that Mr. Chen should not have told Mrs. Li about Mr. Li's secrets so bluntly. She blamed her husband as they were about to sleep. She felt that her husband's attitude was too foolish and could easily lead to two unfortunate outcomes. Directly, the good friendship between Mr. Chen and Mr. Li, which had lasted for years, would immediately be fractured and difficult to restore. Indirectly, it could increase the distance between Mr. and Mrs. Li, or even lead to discord due to excessive admonition. Besides, some people might not understand Mr. Chen's psychology of being upright and loyal, and might mistakenly believe that this kind of assistance to Mrs. Li was a kind of strategy with ulterior motives. Because of these excessive worries, she was very dissatisfied with her husband, even though she and Mrs. Li were also very close friends and she was very willing to help Mrs. Li leave her environment of resentment, grief, and bitterness.

(...) Mr. Chen remained silent. He believed that his actions were very upright, very righteous, very benevolent, and very reasonable. However, he also admitted that he was somewhat foolish. He thought: To save Mr. Li from sinking into the path of delusion and to enable the couple to enjoy the light of love and happiness forever, he had to play the fool once, which might be effective.

Mr. Chen himself had experienced this terrible path of delusion and had acted out many tragic stories because of it. He was an experienced person. The time when a couple is out of harmony is more bitter than suffering from eye inflammation and being exposed to strong light; it is more difficult than a hungry body walking in a dark road and encountering a great storm. He also deeply understood how resentful, grieved, and bitter a woman is when her husband is lost in a path of delusion and she desperately tries to persuade him to turn back, but to no avail, and she cannot get help in an emergency! It is like a husband falling into a mud pit, and his wife is anxious and desperate because she has no way to save him. At this time, if someone is willing to lend her a rope or a bamboo pole so that she can try to help her husband, it is a human sympathy. Since it has no other purpose and does not expect any reward, then it cannot be considered a real fool.

Shanghai Silk Factories Preparing to Resume Operations 121

Silk Public Bonds Have Started to Be Claimed Yesterday

All 106 silk factories in Shanghai, previously due to the depletion of capital, were unable to sustain operations and reduced machines and suspended operations. By the time new cocoons were available, only 36 factories were barely working. Because 4 million yuan of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang silk industry public bond incentive program began to be issued yesterday (31st), each factory owner brought the claim slips to the National Products Bank Silk Public Bond Fund Management Committee to claim bond certificates. However, each factory owner must start operations immediately after receiving the public bonds. Therefore, the 70 or so silk factories that have suspended operations are now hiring craftsmen to repair machinery and purchase raw dry cocoons in preparation for resuming operations. It is expected that about 70% of all silk factories in Shanghai will resume operations before the 15th of this month.

Hardware Niuzhuang Merchants Actively Purchase Hardware Products 123

Since last year, the sales of hardware by Niuzhuang merchants have been very sluggish. The reason is not the lack of business, but the manipulation by the Japanese, which resulted in the majority of market transactions being controlled by the Japanese. Since the boycott, Chinese merchants have switched to handling British and American goods, so the business in Shanghai has turned around. In the past two days, the number of goods purchased has been quite large. Among them, over 500 pieces of 7.5-candareen English steel plates were purchased at a price of 6 taels and 5 candareens. 800 boxes of 90-pound English tinplate were purchased at a price of 14 taels. 214 bars of blue lead were priced at 16 taels. 300 barrels of French "C" nails were priced at 9 taels. It is said that a considerable amount of other old iron products were also purchased.

Local News

Song Ziwen Returns to Beijing Yesterday 144

Minister of Finance Song Ziwen, previously requested a month's leave from the National Government due to his mother's passing to handle funeral affairs, due to many ministry affairs awaiting handling, and needing to prepare for issuing flood relief bonds, therefore yesterday at 3:15 PM, took the special express train departing from the Zhabei Station to Nanjing to return to Beijing to resume duties.

Madam Chiang Song Meiling took the night train to Beijing yesterday.

Disaster Relief from Various Provinces Yesterday 145

Baker Discusses Wuhan Disaster Area Measures

The National Government Flood Relief Committee yesterday released engineer Baker's measures for the Wuhan disaster area, as follows: when the Wuchang embankment broke, over 100,000 Wuhan flood victims all fled to higher ground. These victims varied in wealth, with the majority still able to purchase their own food, while the rest were provided with congee by municipal authorities and charitable organizations to stave off hunger. Currently, local authorities have classified these victims into different levels. Those housed at Wenhua University are mostly factory workers who should be able to find work after the flood recedes. Currently, health workers are keenly aware that many women and children appear to be suffering from hunger, so congee is being distributed, but they often lag behind. A congee kitchen has now been specifically set up for these women and children, so the order in various shelters is currently very good and public funds are not being wasted.

Full Executive Committee Meeting of Emergency Relief Association 146

The Shanghai Fundraising Emergency Flood Relief Association for Various Provinces held a full executive committee meeting yesterday at 4:00 PM at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Attendees included Zhang Qun and his wife, Wang Yiting, Pan Gongzhan, Chu Huiseng, Shi Liangcai, Li Zuyu, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Yansong, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Wang Xiaolai, and over fifty others. Wang Xiaolai was publicly elected as temporary chairman, reporting on letters and the amount of relief funds and grain. They also welcomed the new committee members. Furthermore, the mayor's wife, Madam Zhang, and Dr. Zheng Yuxiu have established a women's group at the Commune Society, which was also welcomed. Next, the meeting discussed ongoing matters: (1) Since the association's establishment, relief funds have been sent in succession, but disaster relief is like fighting a fire, and joint efforts should continue to raise funds to meet urgent needs. Any cases of negligence in delivering relief funds should be pointed out and corrected. (2) Wu Zhihao reported that Zhu Qinglan was previously recommended as a relief distributor, followed by Zhang Zhijiang, Qu Wenliu, etc. However, there should be a report for record for those who have already distributed relief funds, and a request for allocation for those who have not yet distributed. Zhang Qun advocated for expanding the organization of this association, concentrating talent, in order to increase donations. Over a thousand donation books have already been issued, which is not few, but more still need to be issued. Now that the women's group has been established, it can undertake a number of tasks. In terms of entertainment, it can also raise around 100,000 in funds. After the women's group is established, there are many things that should be done, and it is hoped that everyone will contribute their opinions so that they can be written down. We have established this large-scale organization, and if we cannot raise large sums of money, then if the funds raised by the Japanese Chamber of Commerce are more than ours, not only will we let down the disaster victims, but we will also bring international shame. (3) Wu Zhihao proposed nineteen fundraising methods, and recently, together with Pan Gongzhan, will convene various industries to hold a meeting at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. As for the method of raising large sums of money mentioned by Mayor Zhang, it is urgently appropriate to put it forward for discussion. (4) Chu Huiseng reported on the situation of the education sector meeting today. (5) Zhu Qinglan reported that he returned from Hankou three days ago. Roughly, after departing from Nanjing, he passed through Wuhu and Jiujiang to reach Hankou. He did not see the edge of the river along the way, only mountain peaks were exposed, and there was water immediately below the mountains. The rest were small hills and rooftops. After arriving in Hankou, people were travelling everywhere in small boats. Mosquitoes were rampant and the stench was overwhelming. There was no trade in the market. Only the next morning did he see people selling snacks. Large and small households were riding in small wooden basins, vying to buy. Anyone wading in the water had to place what they were carrying on top of their head to avoid getting it wet. There are a total of 104 shelters in Hankou. The food and noodles are still good, and there was only one death, which was immediately buried. If the flooding continues like this, it will inevitably lead to epidemics. Yunmeng County was inundated by the Xiang River, with water ten zhang high. The head of the water rushed past like ten thousand horses, and the people and livestock of the entire county went with the waves. Over a thousand workers in Hankou have no work to do, which feels especially dangerous. Except for a few three- or four-story buildings, the rest are all submerged in water. It is now planned to use large belts to pump water. After returning to Shanghai, he heard that Gaoyou and Shaobo were both submerged, so he immediately took the opportunity to go and inspect. There are over ten breaches in the Grand Canal, and the water is still flooding into the embankments. There is little water inside Gaoyou city, but a lot of water outside the city. The disaster situation is indeed serious. Further north to Jieshou and Sishui, there was also flooding. Baoying was better, but Xinghua was severely flooded. Only below Gaoyou did he gradually see plains. This is the general situation. It is planned to send people to investigate in detail again, and it is especially necessary to fill in the dams first, otherwise the water in the Grand Canal next spring will pour out and there will be no spring plowing. People must be sent there tomorrow. (5) Wang Yiting reported that he went to Hangzhou by early train the day before yesterday to go to the provincial government. He learned that 21 counties have been affected by the disaster, and the mulberry fields in Wuxing, Changxing, Wukang, and Yuhang have all been flooded. Currently, emergency relief is being carried out on one hand, and post-disaster reconstruction is being planned on the other. He then went to the Zhenjiang Civil Affairs Office to liaise, and a temporary Jiangbei Flood Relief Association was established. Shelters have been established in nine places, and more are being added. The number of people is difficult to calculate at the moment, but the relief funds are too small. He hopes that Shanghai will provide assistance. Shanghai has already allocated 20,000. The Civil Affairs Office has received reports of disasters in 54 counties in Jiangsu Province. Xinghua, Jiangpu, Gaoyou, Shaobo, Baoying, Rugao, Funing, Huai'an, Huaiyin, Xiao County, Taixing, Gangshan, Siyang, and Liuhe counties are particularly serious. The provincial government is planning emergency relief. (6) Nie Lusheng reported that the disaster situation in Hunan Province is no less severe than in Hubei. Due to the overflowing of Dongting Lake, 5,000 mu of land in the province cannot be harvested. He hopes that the government will allocate funds to build lake embankments to prevent future disasters. (7) Zhang Xiaolin reported on fundraising methods (currently only over 310,000 yuan has been raised, which is not enough to relieve the disaster victims in Jiangsu Province alone). He is willing to work together with one heart and one mind, and not fall behind the 5 million raised by the Japanese. (7) Shao Ruxin reported that it is planned to raise funds under the item of housing donations. Zhang Qun said that we should not force people to donate. In the past, the government assigned public bonds under the item of housing rent, which caused various troubles. Chu Huiseng suggested asking the Real Estate Association to voluntarily donate. Li Zuyu reported that this was discussed during the design team meeting, and it may not be easy to do. Zhang Xiaolin suggested inviting those with real estate present to take the lead in donating, so as to wait for others to follow suit. Qiaoshaofu donated one month of rent from the Houjiabang property, Du Yuesheng donated two months of rent from the Marong Road property, Wang Xiaolai donated one month of rent from the Taiyuanfang property, Huang Hanzhi donated over 500 taels of rent from one month of property for relief, Wang Boyuan donated over 1,000 yuan of rent from one month of the Yuanyuli, Jingxingli, Danfengli, and Jiufuli properties in Hongkou for relief, and Shi Liangcai donated one month of rent from the Shenbao property for relief. (8) Mayor Zhang's wife, Madam Ma Yuying, reported on (A) holding a tea party to solicit donations, (B) borrowing the Dahua Hotel for two days for a costume dance, and the association will send donation books, (C) inviting Madam Yang Xiaotang, Madam Pan Zhiquan, Madam Guo Anci, and Madam Tan Yasheng to join the dance. Li Yujie proposed donating funds to guests at the exchange. Wen Lanting reported that the exchanges are already proposing to raise funds, and 28,000 yuan has already been turned over. (9) Ren Jinpin and Xu Huiseng proposed telegraphed support for the 80 million public bonds to the Legislative Yuan. A proposal was also made to urge the government to promote Zhang that the proposal to issue public bonds was made by Song Ziwen, and the amount of increase or decrease was also proposed by Song. This is a political issue, which can be conveyed to the Central Relief Committee by Zhu Qinglan. It was resolved to hand it over to the Standing Committee for discussion. (10) Pan Xulun proposed that the association's work should set up more sub-meetings, which was resolved and passed. (11) Wu Zhihao proposed sending a telegram to the National Government to implement the cigarette tax increase case, which was resolved and approved. (12) The chairman asked the various committees to actually attend meetings to work. (13) It was resolved that each group would recommend a director, and it was decided that Wu Yun was recommended as the director of the finance group, Zhang Zhuping of the propaganda group, Zhu Qinglan of the relief group, Xiang Songmao of the medicine delivery group, Wen Lanting of the audit group, Zhang Xiaolin of the fundraising group, Li Zuyu of the design group, and the general affairs group was handed over to the Standing Committee. (14) The proposal to add permanent members to the Standing Committee was decided to add Qu Wenliu and Xu Jingren as executive directors. (15) The propaganda group proposed an external English name as China Flood Famine Society, which was resolved and passed.

Yangzhou Native Place Association Disaster Relief Meeting 147

The Yangzhou Eight Counties Native Place Association convened a full executive committee meeting yesterday, chaired by Shen Dingchen, to discuss (1) The chairman reported that Xue Ganchen and others have raised over 1,000 bags of flour. In addition to being shipped in batches, they are currently continuing to raise more. Furthermore, Gu Deguang and others have jointly purchased cooked food to transport to the disaster area. The association has sent a letter to the Yangzhou Chamber of Commerce requesting their care. (2) Yesterday, the various committee members handed over 2,500 yuan raised in one day to the association. Fundraising is still ongoing, and it was resolved to publish the list of donors in the newspaper every seven days to express gratitude. (3) To handle emergency relief, the various committee members should take special responsibility. Shen Dingchen, Xu Fuchen, and Ruan Mubai were publicly elected as the general affairs group, Li Zhixi and Chen Yangnian as the economic group, and Song Shixiang and Qian Shusheng as the document group. They will go to the association every day to take on their respective responsibilities.

Hubei Relief Association Shanghai Office Established 148

The Hubei Flood Emergency Relief Association's Shanghai fundraising office held a banquet for all sectors of society at the Daguanlou on Fourth Road the day before yesterday (30th) to raise funds for emergency relief. Over 70 guests attended. Chairman Jiang Zuobin attended the meeting despite his illness. He first thanked the guests, saying that although Zuobin had not personally visited the disaster area, he had learned from his fellow villagers in detail that the severity of the disaster was truly unprecedented. The cries of the hungry are everywhere, and relief is urgently needed. Zuobin humbly pleads on behalf of all the suffering compatriots, and deeply hopes that all philanthropists and fellow villagers will do their best to assist and wish them boundless blessings in the future. Then, Mr. Liu Zigu reported on the establishment of this office and the crisis of the Hubei disaster and the disaster victims. After the report, the meeting discussed requesting the press to vigorously promote the disaster situation, preparing for soliciting calligraphy and paintings to help relief, and various fundraising methods. Then, Mr. Wu Guozhen, Director of the Hubei Department of Finance, gave a speech on the disaster situation in Hubei, saying that the long-term cause of the Yangtze River flood was the blockage of the waterway. He noted the Wuhan flood during the Tongzhi period of the Qing Dynasty, which was about 60 years ago, where the water level reached 50 chi and some inches, and was already considered an extremely large flood. Unexpectedly, the water level this year reached over 53 chi, which is truly rare. According to county records, a major flood was seen once 600 years ago. At that time, there was no water level to record, but what can be verified is the saying that only the Turtle and Snake Mountains were visible in Wuhan. The scale of this year's flood is so large that from afar, only the Turtle and Snake Mountains are visible, or even worse than the major flood 600 years ago. It is truly an unprecedented disaster. The disaster area outside the province covers 45 counties. From Hankou to Wuxue, it is a vast expanse of water. As provincial officials, Guozhen and others are at fault for not preventing and rescuing. However, the flood this year was so torrential that rescuing five or six chi, the water reached seven or eight chi and the embankment was breached. It was impossible to prevent. Such a peculiar flood cannot be resisted by human power. There are approximately over ten million disaster victims in the province. The three towns of Wuhan are trapped in deep water. There are approximately over 400,000 people who have no food or support. He hopes that all parties will rush to raise emergency relief to save the current situation. Guozhen and others will again submit a statement to the central government to strive for post-disaster reconstruction. Today, all of you present are working hard for the disaster victims, showing your sincerity. He earnestly asks for your enthusiastic support to save these dying victims. The speech ended at 9 o'clock before everyone dispersed.

Red Cross to Send Personnel to Hankou Today 149

Chairman of the Chinese Red Cross Society, Wang Peiyuan, received a telegram from Li Zushen yesterday, saying: (The water level in Hankou has decreased, and epidemic prevention should be prepared urgently. Please come to Hankou quickly, and everything will be discussed and handled, with utmost anticipation, Li Jin.) He also received a telegram from the Hankou branch saying (Received your letter, knowing that your society will soon organize an epidemic prevention team to come and carry out injection and epidemic prevention work, the sincere, benevolent, and practical relief to the disaster victims is admired, special telegram to welcome, Hankou Red Cross Society President Wang Senfu Director Wang Minpu Yan kowtow). It is learned that the association has designated team leader and medical director Wang Shenghua, deputy team leader and medical director Shi Yunkang, head nurse Jin Weizeng, pharmacist Qin Ruiting, nurses Hu Weisan, Huang Peisheng, and Mao Jinfan, clerks Qian Jiangyuan and Jiang Rusong, and two team members, and will bring over 30 boxes of medicines and depart for Hankou today to handle epidemic prevention and other work.

Zhang Zhijiang's Begging for Relief Telegram 150

To the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association of the Various Provincial Flood Relief Associations, transferred to Mr. Jin Xingren, Mr. Cheng Yiqing, and the gentlemen of both associations. In Jiangdu North, the Shaobo Town Gaoyou area, over ten breaches in the embankment occurred on the 26th of this month. The entire city, the entire town, and the various counties of the Lower River were flooded. Approximately 50,000 to 60,000 residents drowned. Gaoyou City was also flooded on this day, and approximately 70,000 to 80,000 residents drowned. Currently, millions of lives in the downstream counties of the Grand Canal, such as Xinghua, Dongtai, and Suxian, are already in dire straits. This kind of flood is truly rare in thousands of years. The residents of Shaobo and Gaoyou who escaped the danger have climbed onto the city walls and elevated river embankments and rooftops, urgently awaiting rescue. After hearing the news, this office immediately dispatched Councilor Zhang Ruitang, carrying wheel boats, civilian boats, supplies, and many staff and soldiers, to rush to the disaster area day and night for rescue. However, the rescued refugees are crying out for food, urgently awaiting relief. In particular, I urgently request your association to grant more relief to rescue the refugees. Details will be presented in person. Your brother Zhang Zhijiang Zhang Shusheng kowtows.

County Party Headquarters Organizes Disaster Relief Donation Team 151

The Shanghai County Party Headquarters recently organized a disaster relief donation team to carry out fundraising. All organizational methods and the leaders and deputy leaders of each team have been approved by the 12th Executive Committee. The details are compiled below:

▲Organizational Methods Article 1: All comrades in Shanghai County will organize a fundraising team to relieve the national flood disaster under the leadership of the County Executive Committee. Article 2: The team is named the Shanghai County Disaster Relief Donation Team of the Jiangsu Provincial Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang. Article 3: The team is divided into six major teams and one special team, with a general team leader in charge. Article 4: The leaders and deputy leaders of the six teams will be appointed by the County Executive Committee from comrades in each district who are enthusiastic, hardworking, and have a reputation of integrity in the local area. Article 5: The leader of the special team will be appointed by the County Executive Committee. Article 6: The members of each team will be composed of party members and staff members of the association from the entire county. Article 7: After receiving the donation booklet, each team member will report to the team leader every three days. Each team leader will report to the general team leader every week, without delay. Article 8: The general team leader will collect the donations, issue receipts, and immediately deposit the funds into the designated bank. Article 9: The fundraising period is temporarily set for one month and may be extended if necessary. Article 10: The general team leader is responsible for convening the teams to plan fundraising and supervise and inspect them at any time. Article 11: The team shall not spend public funds. Travel expenses may be requested from the County Executive Committee when necessary. Article 12: Those teams with excellent fundraising results will be awarded honorary prizes by the County Executive Committee. Those with poor performance will be punished. Article 13: The reward and punishment methods will be determined separately. Article 14: If any team member is found to be engaged in private gain, fraud, or embezzlement of donations, they will be severely punished after investigation. Article 15: These methods will be implemented upon resolution by the County Executive Committee.

▲Team Leader Names General Team Leader: Lü Zhe. Team 1: Leader Wu Jingqing, Deputy Shen Jing. Team 2: Leader Gu Yunru, Deputy Ding Borong. Team 3: Leader Yang Zhuoyun, Deputy Zhang Yi. Team 4: Leader Huo Guiliang, Deputy Jin Yongxin. Team 5: Leader Ge Xiusheng, Deputy Xiao Jianxun. Team 6: Leader Wang Chengyao, Deputy Zhang Jingye. Special Team: Leader Jiang Yanqiu, Deputy Peng Liren.

▲Fundraising Declaration This year's continuous rain has caused disasters, and floods have overflowed. Areas such as Jiangsu, Anhui, Hunan, and Hubei have been submerged for months, and the floodwaters have not subsided. The Yellow River has also burst, causing dangerous situations in Hebei and Shandong. Levees have collapsed in Gao and Shao, one after another. The affected areas span sixteen provinces, with sixty million victims. The dead are buried in the bellies of fish, and floating corpses drift with the waves. The living eke out an existence, sleeping in the open air and eating in the wind. Seedlings are submerged, livestock and people drift away, cities have become swamps, and fertile fields are now lakes. This unprecedented catastrophe is unparalleled in history. Currently, hundreds of millions of disaster victims urgently need relief. Driven by compassion, the members of this association cannot bear to sit idly by. We have organized a disaster relief donation team, appealing to compatriots from all walks of life to have the heart of those who are already hungry and drowning, to uphold the righteousness of being crowned and clothed, to generously open their wallets, and enthusiastically contribute. Let's gather sand to form a tower, collect fur to make a robe, so that hundreds of millions of wailing disaster victims can return to their mats as soon as possible. We are extremely eager to implore and pray. This declaration is hereby made, and we hope for your public understanding.

▲Start of Fundraising After the team is established, it is planned to start work immediately and raise funds in various districts.

Xiang Xiang Pleads for the Disaster Victims 152

When Mr. Xiang Xiang was in New York, USA, he had a previous acquaintance with President Hoover. Due to the severity of the floods in the country, he recently sent a telegram to Washington in his private capacity, asking for surplus cotton and wheat to help with disaster relief. The main idea of his original telegram is translated as follows: (Omitted above) Hot and turbulent weather waves reverse and attack the Great Snow Mountains of the Western Sichuan Plateau, flowing eastward. The river basins of major rivers, taking the Chinese plains as their outlet, overflow simultaneously. Combined with the impact of tides and flash floods, dams are completely destroyed, and houses are gone. The disaster area covers sixteen provinces, and 50 million disaster victims are immersed in water, crying out and waiting to die. This is truly an unprecedented catastrophe in our country. Our government and people have already cooperated in providing urgent relief, but because the disaster area is vast, we fear that our efforts may fall short. In the blink of an eye, winter is approaching, making hunger and cold even more difficult. Without large-scale work, it will be difficult to achieve effective results. This year, Germany faced a gold shortage and was granted a one-year postponement of war debts, allowing them to breathe a sigh of relief. This righteous act has been admired by the world. Currently, our country is facing an unprecedented flood disaster, which is of even greater importance. We also implore the benevolent people of this God, to advocate to all sectors of society, to make a grand wish to use your country's surplus cotton and wheat to provide as much assistance as possible, and to unite philanthropists around the world to carry out large-scale relief and direct reconstruction, further promoting the spirit of a great nation. Charity knows no borders. Therefore, I dare to plead for the lives of 50 million disaster victims. (Omitted below)

▲Hui Ning Fellow Villagers Disaster Relief Meeting

The Shanghai Hui Ning Fellow Villagers Association held its first executive committee meeting of the Disaster Relief Preparatory Committee the other day. Chairman Hu Junhua reported on the first plenary committee meeting and the process of appointing personnel for each department. Then, the following proposals were discussed and resolved: (1) Passed the association's telegram requesting relief. (2) Passed the fundraising announcement. (3) Designated the Anhui Bank in this city, the Taiping Bank, and the association's office as fundraising collection points. (4) Committee member Li Zhenya proposed that the following items should be presented to the former provincial government for implementation in the disaster-stricken counties: A. Exemption of grain tribute in the disaster-stricken counties. B. Request the provincial government officials, from the chairman downwards, to donate their emoluments to help with disaster relief to set an example. C. Issue disaster relief public bonds quickly to meet emergency needs. D. An order should be issued to all counties to earnestly appease the disaster victims and avoid inciting civil unrest. In addition, Committee member Zhang Yizhai proposed that the National Government and the Control Yuan should be requested to investigate and punish officials who were derelict in their duties in protecting against the floods in various provinces this time, in order to appease the public. All were passed. (5) Send a letter of condolence to the affected fellow villagers in Wuhan and urgently prepare corresponding relief measures. (6) Report the disaster situation in each county obtained by the association to the Anhui Flood Disaster Relief Association and the flood disaster relief associations in various provinces for collective handling. (7) Send a letter to each disaster area to report the disaster situation in the form of a list to the association for record, publish photos in newspapers, and send a letter to the Hui Ning Guild Hall to request all directors to join the association for full cooperation. The meeting adjourned at about 8 o'clock.

Various Circles Enthusiastically Help Disaster Relief

Lianyi Charity Association Has Huge Amount of Flour and Cotton Clothes for Distribution ▲ The Lianyi Charity Association has raised 5,000 bags of flour and more than 30,000 yuan in cash. A large number of cotton clothes have been made and transported to disaster areas in various provinces for distribution.

▲Pawnshop Industry Acknowledges Donation of 20,000 Yuan The Pawnshop Industry Association held a meeting yesterday with Fu Zuoheng as chairman. After discussion, it was decided that the pawnshop industry, including shop assistants, would publicly donate 20,000 yuan.

▲Cotton Fabric Industry Has Collected 4,000 to 5,000 Yuan The Cotton Fabric Industry Association held a committee meeting the other day to discuss relief measures and decided to solicit donations from all colleagues. It started yesterday afternoon and collected 4,000 to 5,000 yuan in half a day. It is expected that there will be even better results tomorrow and the day after.

▲Biscuit and Bread Industry Meeting for Disaster Relief The Confectionery, Candy, and Canned Food Industry Association held a standing committee meeting yesterday with Zhang Yichen as chairman. They discussed measures. In addition to the 20 large boxes of canned pickles donated by the Dalu Factory, 500 pounds of biscuits from the Taichang Company, and cash from the Likang Factory, the rest are still being solicited.

▲Antique Guild Raises Funds for Disaster Relief The Antique Industry Association held a general meeting of representatives yesterday and decided to organize a fundraising team. In addition to the thousands of dollars pledged on the spot, it was also decided that from today to the 7th, the proceeds from the theatrical performances in this market will be used as donations, and during these seven days, the commissions earned by the industry will be used for disaster relief.

▲Fresh Fish Industry Launches Emergency Relief The Fresh Fish Trade Association sent letters to all members yesterday, stating that the association had decided that all firms and shops in the industry would donate all commissions earned from September 1st to 5th to the Shanghai Disaster Relief Emergency Relief Association for Various Provinces at the Renji Charity Hall on Yunnan Road in this city, so that they can be distributed to the disaster areas as soon as possible.

▲China General Edison Company Employees Assist Jiangsu Relief Again All employees of the China General Edison Company in the South City had previously raised a large sum of money to help with disaster relief. Now they are willing to donate the money from the company's usual banquets for all colleagues during the summer and autumn festivals this year, estimated at 1,000 yuan, to the disaster relief efforts in this province. They have jointly requested the company authorities to directly hand it over to the Jiangsu Yizhen Association for distribution.

▲Results of the Disaster Relief Rally at the Central Sports Ground Mr. Haig, the manager of the Central Sports Ground, held a disaster relief rally the other night. As a result, the ticket sales amounted to 2,159 yuan, and the flower sales amounted to 747 yuan. The stadium also donated another 1,094 yuan, totaling 4,000 yuan, which has been handed over by Zhu Boquan of the Central Bank to the Continental Bank for forwarding to the Emergency Relief Association.

▲Fufeng Paper Company Donates 800 Yuan in Commissions to Aid Relief Fufeng Paper Company has been donating 10% of its door sales since August 27th, totaling more than 800 yuan as of the other day, which will be sent to the Disaster Relief Association for forwarding.

▲Dafeng Silk and Satin Store Donates 500 Yuan The Dafeng Silk and Satin Store specially donated 300 yuan, and the store's colleagues jointly donated 200 yuan, totaling 500 yuan, which has been sent to the Emergency Relief Association for distribution.

▲Problems Arise with Relief Grain Arriving in Hankou Yesterday, Committee Member Zhu received a telegram from Hankou, saying, "To Mr. Zhu Ziqiao, the cakes loaded on the Changsha ship are severely moldy and cannot be used. The cakes not yet loaded in Shanghai do not need to be transported anymore. Can you please inspect them personally to ensure hygiene? Please telegraph Lao Wai and decide how to proceed." Li Jin

▲Xu Jianping Donates 500 Yuan to Aid Relief Xu Jianping had a son last month and specially transferred the 500 yuan from the noodle banquet to emergency relief.

▲Fundraising Entertainment News The China Jiande Association has been preparing for the National Flood Disaster Relief Entertainment Convention for days, and the work is extremely intense. Peking Opera is being handled by Mr. Wang Xiaolai and Tu Kaizheng, and the progress of various famous amateurs is very satisfactory. On the music side, Mr. Huang Shaohua and Wu Chengbiao are in charge. Those who have already agreed to participate include the China Music Association, the South China Music Association, the Jingwu Association Cantonese Music Group, the Sanyu Music Association, the China Harmonica Association, and the Songbai Music Society, a total of six groups. The Star Song and Dance and Kun Opera groups are being handled by Mr. Zhou Shixun and others, and the results are also very satisfactory.

▲Hongchang Factory Donates Commissions to Aid Relief Mr. Fu Zhiyuan, the director and general manager of Hongchang Advertising Construction Factory, and Mr. Fu Huaxin, the manager, decided to donate 20% of the business income in September to aid disaster relief.

▲Tongyi Yarn Factory Employees Donate Salary to Aid Relief All workers of the Tongyi Yarn Factory, initiated by the 13th branch of the 3rd district and the Shanghai 3rd District Cotton Textile Industry Union, donated one day's wages, which can amount to about 1,500 yuan. In addition, all employees of the Tongyi Yarn Factory donated three days' salaries, which can amount to about 400 yuan. Once collected, they will be sent to the disaster relief agency for distribution to the disaster areas.

▲Local Court President and Police Deduct Salaries to Aid Relief All presidents and police officers of the Shanghai Local Court each deducted one yuan from their salaries yesterday, totaling 30 yuan, to donate to the Flood Disaster Relief Committee.

▲Lecture Group Donates Ticket Sales to Aid Relief The ticket sales from the disaster relief entertainment event held the other day have been handed over to the Shanghai Bank and credited to the Shanghai Emergency Relief Association for Various Provinces for the purpose of relieving disaster victims.

▲Rickshaw Pullers Form Disaster Relief Association Rickshaw pullers in this city held a disaster relief meeting at the Minli Elementary School on Meiyuan Road yesterday, performing the ceremony as usual. Wang Qiaoping was publicly elected as chairman. As a result, Wang Zhiping, Bian Qinghong, Zhu Fengxiang, Cang Gongwen, Zhu Richang, Xiao Zhishan, Bian Weisong, Meng Jinchen, and Liu Zhuanjun were publicly elected as nine people responsible for handling the matter. They decided to divide into three groups: Wang Zhiping as the director of documentation, and Meng Jinchen and Liu Fuzhun as clerks; Zhu Fengxiang as the director of publicity, and Xiao Zhishan and Zhu Richang as clerks; Bian Qinghong as the director of fundraising, and Bian Weisong and Cang Gongwen as clerks. They will solicit donations separately and hand over the funds raised to the Emergency Disaster Relief Association.

▲Buddhist Lay Forest Raises Funds for Disaster Relief The Zhabei Buddhist Lay Forest Disaster Relief Association has now raised more than 3,000 yuan, which will be gradually handed over to the Jiangsu Disaster Relief Association and the China Jisheng Association for distribution. It has also launched a campaign to collect dried pot scrapings (rice crust) to be sent to the Yangzhou disaster area for distribution.

▲Puyi Society Staff Donates Monthly Salary to Aid Relief In view of the urgent need for disaster relief at home and abroad, the staff of the Christian Puyi Society are specially donating their monthly salaries, stipulating that those with a monthly salary of less than 50 yuan donate 5%, those with a salary of less than 100 yuan donate 10%, and those with a salary of more than 100 yuan but less than 300 yuan donate 20%. The funds will be sent to the Relief Affairs Committee for distribution that day. The staff of the affiliated institutions have also been solicited separately and will be collected before the 15th of this month.

▲Embroidery Industry Donates Commissions The Embroidery Industry Association held an executive committee meeting yesterday. As a result, all shops in the industry will donate 10% of their business income. Those who have already acknowledged the donation include Hengzhangtai, Wanliyuan, and Xintaixiang.

After the hurricane this time, Shao Bo and Gao You suffered

Page 18

another major flood, with fields and homes submerged, people scattered and displaced, and deaths piled high. Relief efforts are underway, but Shanghai's inland and offshore merchant ships have also been greatly affected. The information heard is recorded separately below:

▲Small Steamers Suspend Operations to Rescue Disaster Victims This time, the embankment at Shao You broke, causing many deaths. The disaster has also spread to Dongtai and Xinghua. There are still many disaster victims living on high mounds and treetops, waiting to be rescued. The Jiangsu Provincial Government has ordered the Emergency Relief Association to requisition small steamers and civilian boats to go to the Shao You area to transport and rescue refugees. The Shanghai Merchants Steam Navigation Company and other inland river shipping companies have resumed services on the Suzhou-Hangzhou line, Changli line, Xi Li line, Xi Cheng line, and Xi Xuan line. All small steamers have been temporarily seized by the Water Disaster Relief Association. The company's ships have also been requisitioned and sent to Shao You, Dongtai, and other places to transport disaster victims to ports such as Yangzhou, Zhenjiang, and Shanghai. Therefore, small steamers on the inland rivers of Jiangsu Province, which had been suspended from July 6th to the end of August and had just resumed operations once or twice, are now completely suspended again. Yesterday, the Shen Su line's small steamer was afraid of being seized en route, so although the cargo was fully loaded, it did not dare to set sail.

▲Losses in Inland Waterway Shipping This time, the major flood disaster in Jiangsu and Zhejiang caused the Shanghai inland river shipping companies to suspend operations for two months. The other day, when the strong wind and rain occurred, the Merchants Steam Navigation Company's wharves in Zhenjiang and Hangzhou were also destroyed by the flood. Yesterday, Mr. Gu of the company told reporters that the total loss of the Merchants Steam Navigation Company's head office and branch offices in the inland rivers due to the major flood disaster in July and August reached 100,000 yuan, and there is still no hope of resuming operations. Other shipping companies have also suffered the same losses. It is estimated that the total loss of the various shipping companies due to this natural disaster is at least 200,000 to 300,000 yuan, which is truly a major catastrophe for the shipping industry.

▲Yichang Steamer to Sail to Shanghai Today The Taikoo Yichang Steamer ran aground in Hongguan Bay outside Xiamen during the first hurricane on August 14th. It was able to sail out after 12 hours. After arriving in Xiamen, it loaded cargo and passengers and sailed to Shanghai on the 24th. It encountered a second hurricane while sailing on the sea off Fuzhou. Fortunately, the shipowner took precautions, and the ship ran aground on the sand in the shallow waters of the Min Sea. On the 26th, after the wind subsided and the waves calmed, it managed to sail out on its own. Because the hull was slightly damaged, it returned to Xiamen. Yesterday, the company received a telegram from the Yichang Steamer, reporting that it is now undergoing minor repairs in Xiamen. The cargo and passengers were not damaged during the grounding. After the repairs are completed, it will immediately sail back to Shanghai.

▲Guangli Steamer Fortunately Escaped Danger The Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Guangli Steamer encountered a strong wind while sailing from Shanghai to Fujian on the sea off Wenzhou. The shipowner, Teng Shibiao, quickly dropped both anchors into the sea to anchor and avoid the wind. Unexpectedly, the wind and waves were too strong, and the ship's hull was pushed, causing it to run aground on the beach. The shipowner sent out a distress signal. At that time, the Sanbei's Wanxiang Steamer and the Japanese ship Longchang Maru passed by, but both were unable to come to the rescue due to the dangerous wind and waves. The passengers in the ship were extremely panicked. Fortunately, the business director and the naval police on board tried their best to comfort and maintain order, which turned danger into safety and prevented any accidents. When the wind gradually subsided and the waves also stopped on the 26th, the ship was able to sail out of the shallows with the tide due to the shipowner's efforts in the face of difficulties. It has now safely arrived in Fuzhou, and the cargo and passengers are all safe. A special telegram was sent yesterday, reporting that it will leave Fujian and return to Shanghai immediately. After arriving in Shanghai, the bottom of the ship will be inspected for any damage to facilitate repairs.

▲Inventory of Water Damage to Warehouse Goods Due to the major flood in this city the other day, the warehouses in Pudong and Puxi and along the Suzhou River, as well as the docks and police stations of various shipping companies, were flooded. After days of pumping and drainage, the water has been completely discharged. The various shipping companies have identified a total of 160 large and small warehouses that were flooded, and the total value of the cargo damaged by water is estimated at 750,000 yuan. Various warehouses are still in the process of clearing and inspecting the goods these days.

Stop Entertainment

and Lower the Flag to Half-Mast

According to Article 6 of the State Funeral Law, on the day of the state funeral, all civil servants must wear black gauze armbands, the whole country must stop entertainment, and all groups, shops, and residents must lower the flag to half-mast for one day to express mourning. This order."

Bank of China Establishes Osaka Branch 154

Talks with Zhang Gongquan

Opening Scheduled for Today

The Bank of China has recently established a branch in Osaka, Japan, and is scheduled to open today. The manager of the Osaka branch is Ju Yirong, the current deputy manager of the Bank of China's Shanghai branch, and the assistant manager is Zheng Boling of the Kobe Netherlands Bank. Both are familiar with Osaka's business. A reporter from the Huadong News Agency visited Mr. Zhang Gongquan, the president of the bank, in his office yesterday, and he gave the following statement. According to Mr. Zhang, China and Japan are separated by a strip of water, and transportation is convenient. Moreover, due to various historical relationships, commerce between the two countries is particularly developed. Judging from the recent five-year customs reports, it is of great benefit to Japanese merchants engaged in Sino-Japanese trade. Furthermore, among Japan's exports to China, cotton yarn and cloth account for the largest proportion, followed by manufactured goods such as seaweed, medicines, steel, and machinery. Among China's exports to Japan, rapeseed, hemp, medicinal seeds, leather, and hair are mostly raw materials. Osaka is the center of Japan's industry and is close to Kobe. All cargo handling is concentrated here, so Chinese merchants gather here. According to recent estimates, there are about 3,000 Chinese merchants in Osaka, representing various industries, mostly yarn, cloth, and sundry goods merchants. According to the bank's estimates, the total amount of this direct trade is around 120 to 30 million Japanese yen per year. The inconveniences felt due to the lack of a domestic financial institution to mediate this large amount are as follows: (1) Differences in language and customs often hinder transactions. (2) Japanese merchant banks are inevitably unfamiliar with the situation of Chinese merchants, and sometimes the conditions are too harsh, making it impossible for Chinese merchants to meet them one by one. (3) Japanese or other foreign banks do not understand the true situation of Chinese merchants. Therefore, when there is a risk, they all rush to close accounts, even cutting off contact altogether, which causes Chinese merchants great pain. (4) Chinese merchants come from all over the country, especially from the north. Japanese merchant banks only handle remittances to major commercial ports and cannot penetrate the interior of China. Therefore, remittances are still inconvenient, and there are many losses. In order to alleviate the above-mentioned difficulties, Chinese merchants in Japan all hope that there will be a bank with strong capital, outstanding credit, branches all over the country, and smooth remittances to establish a branch in Osaka to facilitate turnover and achieve mutual benefits with Chinese merchants. Furthermore, considering the content of Sino-Japanese trade, between Japan and central and southern China, China exports more to Japan and Japan imports less to China. As for Japan and northern China, China exports less to Japan and Japan imports more to China. The reason why China imports more from Japan lies in the fact that the north exports less and imports more. The reason why the north exports less and imports more lies in the inconvenient transportation in the north. The import of local products from the north passes through Gansu, Shaanxi, Shanxi, and Hebei. Apart from the occasional automobile roads and boat transportation, the rest of the transportation completely relies on the power of people and animals. It often takes years to reach, which greatly hinders the sale of goods. If there is a bank to provide long-term assistance, the export of local products will definitely develop due to increased convenience. In order to satisfy the hopes of Chinese merchants and promote the development of exports, the Bank of China has the qualifications for this purpose. Therefore, after repeated negotiations by Yu in the past and with the assistance of Japanese colleagues, we finally obtained the understanding of the authorities and obtained a license in February of this year. After several months of preparation, we are scheduled to open tomorrow (i.e. today). This will not only benefit commerce, but also bring glory to the country's image.

Tao Baichuan's Speech on National Self-Salvation and Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese 157

The Day Before Yesterday at the Great China Broadcasting Station

(National News Agency) The Third District Party Headquarters of this city, in order to promote party ideology, invites prominent figures from the party and government circles to give lectures on the Three Principles of the People every Sunday. The day before yesterday, they specially invited Tao Baichuan, a standing committee member of the Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters, to give a speech at the Great China Electrical Company's radio broadcasting station on Nanjing Road, entitled "National Self-Salvation and Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese." The following is an excerpt of the main points of his speech: China is a semi-colonial country, even worse than the annexed Korea and Annam. Because Korea and Annam are only slaves to one country, Japan or France, but China is not; it has to be a slave to many countries. Therefore, in order for the Chinese nation to be independent and equal, and to break away from the oppression of imperialism, the 400 million people must rise up and save themselves; they cannot rely solely on the Chinese Kuomintang or the National Government. China's biggest enemy at present is Japanese imperialism. Because their industries and commerce are very developed, their capital is abundant, and domestic production exceeds demand, they are trying their best to expand abroad. However, the countries of Europe and America have no room for them to intervene, so they have no choice but to attack China, whose industry and commerce are underdeveloped and whose capital is declining in the East. Recently, because Japan instigated Koreans to massacre our overseas Chinese, the national sentiment boiled over, and anti-Japanese and aid-to-overseas-Chinese associations were organized to implement boycotts of Japanese goods and economic severance with Japan. However, we cannot entrust the responsibility of defeating Japanese imperialism completely to the staff of the anti-Japanese and aid-to-overseas-Chinese associations; all 400 million people must take responsibility and attack Japan in unison in order to eliminate Japanese imperialism, and then the Chinese nation can be saved, and so on.

Notices for Collection of Municipal Donations Should be Uniform for Chinese and Foreigners 162

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association Sends Another Letter to the Public Works Department

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Public Works Department yesterday, stating: "To the honorable department, according to a letter from taxpayer Mr. Ye, the Public Works Department's collection of municipal general donations from our Chinese people is unfairly biased. No prior notice is issued for consultation. Your council resolved that future payments should be made within 14 days after receiving a formal notice from the Public Works Department. Your council published a notice to the citizens in the newspaper on May 28. On July 1, the Public Works Department published a notice in the newspaper, canceling the notice. Regardless of Chinese or foreigners, future donations will be collected after the Public Works Department publishes the date in the newspaper, and people should go to pay on their own. Up to now, no response has been seen from your council. Yesterday (August 26), the bureau sent Westerners to our office to collect donations. In order to implement your council's resolution, I refused to pay. Unexpectedly, the bureau suddenly sent a notice today. This is inconsistent and contradictory, and it is clearly discriminatory against the Chinese. Your council is a representative of hundreds of thousands of taxpayers in our city. What is the course of action for the above notice? I think you have already set a concrete plan. Please give instructions so that we can follow them. I support your council's power. Even if there is any sacrifice to benefit our taxpayers, I will not hesitate." It also attached a copy of the donation notice to the meeting for investigation. Regarding the collection of municipal general donations, your bureau should issue notices uniformly for both Chinese and Western-style houses to show equal treatment. Our association has repeatedly sent letters to implement this. Regarding the 14-day deadline for the notice received by our association, the red pencil has already been crossed out. Whether other Western-style houses are handled uniformly, please pay special attention to your bureau. According to the letter, your bureau has not yet handled the issuance of notices for Chinese-style houses uniformly, which is not consistent with the statement of "no discriminatory treatment." It is appropriate to send a letter to your bureau requesting prompt handling to avoid complications.

The Customs Office is Building New Warships 163

Chinese Crew Members Will Be Used

The Jianghai Customs Office has three patrol ships, Liuxing, Chuantiao, etc., which are responsible for patrolling the coastal ports to prevent smuggling of goods to evade customs duties. They also often set out to assist in rescuing merchant ships in distress. Now, the Jianghai Customs Office is adding a new-style patrol ship at the Rui Rong Factory in this port. The engine has been converted to use fuel. The hull of the ship has been completed and will soon be launched. Currently, the senior crew members of the three ships are all Westerners. Now that the new ship has been completed, the Customs Office has decided to completely replace them with domestic navigation professionals, from the captain down, as a sign of reclaiming navigation rights.
